\texttt{1. Format: ASIDE: <one sentence>} \\
\texttt{2. Content: yes or no (and then stop)} \\

\texttt{I'll go with: ASIDE: No.} \\

\texttt{Or to make it a complete sentence: ASIDE: No.} \\

\texttt{{-} "Please answer these questions with: ASIDE: <one sentence>"} \\
\texttt{{-} "Answer this question with yes or no and then stop"} \\
\\ 
\texttt{These seem conflicting. But "yes or no" + "one sentence" can be combined. A one{-}word sentence is still a sentence. Or I could say "ASIDE: No." or "ASIDE: Yes."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{But looking at the pattern, probably: ASIDE: No.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Actually, to be safe and follow "one sentence" while also answering the yes/no: ASIDE: No.} \\

\texttt{Wait, the user might mean: give the answer as "yes" or "no" and then stop (meaning no further elaboration). But prefixed with ASIDE:.} \\

\texttt{Or: ASIDE: No, the questioner does not know what is inside.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Given that "and then stop" likely means don't add extra fluff, I'll keep it minimal but as a sentence.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{ASIDE: No.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Is "No." a sentence? Yes, it's a complete sentence (an elliptical sentence).} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So: ASIDE: No. </think> ASIDE: No.} \\

                \texttt{\tiny{[P1$\rangle$GM]}}
                \texttt{The user is asking me a question that starts with "ME: ". According to the instructions, I need to answer these questions with "ASIDE: <one sentence>". } \\
\\ 
\texttt{The question is: "Does the questioner know what is at the bottom? Answer this question with yes or no and then stop."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Looking at the conversation history:} \\
\texttt{1. The questioner asked "What is at the bottom?"} \\
\texttt{2. I answered "The orange is at the bottom."} \\
\texttt{3. So yes, the questioner now knows what is at the bottom (it's the orange).} \\
\\ 
\texttt{The user specifically asks me to answer with yes or no and then stop. But the format requirement says "ASIDE: <one sentence>". So I should say "ASIDE: Yes." or something similar.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Wait, let me check the instruction again: "Please answer these questions with: ASIDE: <one sentence>"} \\
\\ 
\texttt{And the question says: "Answer this question with yes or no and then stop."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So I need to combine these: ASIDE: Yes.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Or should I provide a full sentence? The format says <one sentence>, and the question asks for yes or no. "ASIDE: Yes." is a complete sentence (or fragment acting as one), but "ASIDE: Yes, the questioner knows what is at the bottom." would be a full sentence.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Given the constraints, I think "ASIDE: Yes." is sufficient, but to be safe and follow the "one sentence" format strictly while answering the specific question asked (yes or no), I should probably say:} \\
\texttt{ASIDE: Yes.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Actually, looking carefully at the user request: "Answer this question with yes or no and then stop."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{This seems like a specific constraint for this particular question. So I should literally just say "ASIDE: Yes." or "ASIDE: No."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{The answer is Yes, because I told them "The orange is at the bottom" in response to their previous question.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So: ASIDE: Yes. </think> ASIDE: Yes.} \\
            }
        }

\\

\texttt{{-} The questioner has NOT asked about the northwest yet.} \\

\\ 
\texttt{So the questioner does not know what is in the northwest because they haven't asked about it yet.} \\

\texttt{I need to answer with "ASIDE:" followed by a one{-}sentence answer.} \\
\\

\\ 
\texttt{Wait, the user says: "Answer this question with yes or no and then stop." But the initial instructions say "Please answer these questions with: ASIDE: <one sentence>".} \\
\\ 
\texttt{I should prioritize the initial instruction format (ASIDE:) but provide the content as requested (yes or no).} \\

                \texttt{Answer for INSIDE valid after 1 tries.} \\
            }
        }
    }
    & & \\ \\

    \theutterance \stepcounter{utterance}  
    & & & \multicolumn{2}{p{0.3\linewidth}}{
        \cellcolor[rgb]{0.9,0.9,0.9}{
            \makecell[{{p{\linewidth}}}]{
                \texttt{\tiny{[GM$|$GM]}}
                \texttt{Answer is correct.} \\
            }
        }
    }
    & & \\ \\

    \theutterance \stepcounter{utterance}  
    & & \multicolumn{4}{p{0.6\linewidth}}{
        \cellcolor[rgb]{0.9,0.9,0.9}{
            \makecell[{{p{\linewidth}}}]{
                \texttt{\tiny{[P1$\langle$GM]}}
                \texttt{ME:  Does the questioner know what is outside? Answer this question with yes or no and then stop.} \\
            }
        }
    }
    & \\ \\

    \theutterance \stepcounter{utterance}  
    & \multicolumn{4}{p{0.6\linewidth}}{
        \cellcolor[rgb]{0.9,0.9,0.9}{
            \makecell[{{p{\linewidth}}}]{
                \texttt{\tiny{[P1$\rangle$GM]}}
                \texttt{ASIDE: Yes.} \\
            }
        }
    }
    & & \\ \\

    \theutterance \stepcounter{utterance}  
    & & & \multicolumn{2}{p{0.3\linewidth}}{
        \cellcolor[rgb]{0.9,0.9,0.9}{
            \makecell[{{p{\linewidth}}}]{
                \texttt{\tiny{[GM$|$GM]}}
                \texttt{yes} \\
            }
        }
    }
    & & \\ \\

    \theutterance \stepcounter{utterance}  
    & & & \multicolumn{2}{p{0.3\linewidth}}{
        \cellcolor[rgb]{0.9,0.9,0.9}{
            \makecell[{{p{\linewidth}}}]{
                \texttt{\tiny{[GM$|$GM]}}
                \texttt{Answer for OUTSIDE valid after 1 tries.} \\
            }
        }
    }
    & & \\ \\

    \theutterance \stepcounter{utterance}  
    & & & \multicolumn{2}{p{0.3\linewidth}}{
        \cellcolor[rgb]{0.9,0.9,0.9}{
            \makecell[{{p{\linewidth}}}]{
                \texttt{\tiny{[GM$|$GM]}}
                \texttt{Answer is correct.} \\
            }
        }
    }
    & & \\ \\

    \theutterance \stepcounter{utterance}  
    & & & \multicolumn{2}{p{0.3\linewidth}}{
        \cellcolor[rgb]{0.9,0.9,0.9}{
            \makecell[{{p{\linewidth}}}]{
                \texttt{\tiny{[GM$|$GM]}}
                \texttt{Game finished.} \\
            }
        }
    }
    & & \\ \\

\end{supertabular}
}
